  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer12349178357760655242">Nothing has been the same since Caleb Becker left a party drunk, got behind the wheel, and hit Maggie Armstrong. Even after months of painful physical therapy, Maggie walks with a limp. Her social life is nil and a scholarship to study abroad—her chance to escape everyone and their pitying stares—has been canceled.<br/><br/>After a year in juvenile jail, Caleb’s free . . . if freedo</span>
  <span id="freeText12349178357760655242" style="display:none">Nothing has been the same since Caleb Becker left a party drunk, got behind the wheel, and hit Maggie Armstrong. Even after months of painful physical therapy, Maggie walks with a limp. Her social life is nil and a scholarship to study abroad—her chance to escape everyone and their pitying stares—has been canceled.<br /><br />After a year in juvenile jail, Caleb’s free . . . if freedom means endless nagging from a transition coach and the prying eyes of the entire town. Coming home should feel good, but his family and ex-girlfriend seem like strangers.<br /><br />Caleb and Maggie are outsiders, pigeon-holed as "criminal" and "freak." Then the truth emerges about what really happened the night of the accident and, once again, everything changes. It’s a bleak and tortuous journey for Caleb and Maggie, yet they end up finding comfort and strength from a surprising source: each other.</span>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">o..0? This is a place to find books! If there was an actor to play Caleb I would try to find a cute tough 'wrestle player' looking- overprotective bro<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">o..0? This is a place to find books! If there was an actor to play Caleb I would try to find a cute tough 'wrestle player' looking- overprotective brother dude that wants to do good but bad things seem to find him no matter what everywhere he goes type of dude. Very sweet and overprotective for those of who he cares about. Sometimes taking the blame and guilt on himself just to make sure the ones he loves are okay. And yet at the end of the day he's heartbroken and sad and frustrated. Good luck! I'd love a short story if your talking about making one about Caleb? o.0 If so that'd be great! <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer492436943" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1325018594501757609">You know your Monday night is going downhill when you're stuck weeping over a cliffhanger.<br/><br/>I mean, this is the last straw in the haystack. The last chocolate in the box. The icing on the cake. The hole in the piñata. <br/><br/>I get that there will be cliffhangers. What I don't get is why only I ever seemed to be constantly plagued by them! 4/5 times, a book I will pick up will go something like this:<br/><br/>Book: Introducing a delicious guy character with soulful eyes and a great sense of humour<br/>Book: Ooh look - h</span>
  <span id="freeText1325018594501757609" style="display:none">You know your Monday night is going downhill when you're stuck weeping over a cliffhanger.<br /><br />I mean, this is the last straw in the haystack. The last chocolate in the box. The icing on the cake. The hole in the piñata. <br /><br />I get that there will be cliffhangers. What I don't get is why only I ever seemed to be constantly plagued by them! 4/5 times, a book I will pick up will go something like this:<br /><br />Book: Introducing a delicious guy character with soulful eyes and a great sense of humour<br />Book: Ooh look - heroine with a backbone! <br />Book: Her and the guy aren't getting along...obviously this means they are MEANT FOR EACHOTHER<br />Book: Insert awesome situations that make you wish you had this life<br />Book: *Spend several moments sniffling over your sad, lonely life*<br />Book: BREAK UP/CRYING IN THE RAIN SCENE <br />Book: Stop listening to Taylor Swift on repeat and watch as they mope for days<br />Book: Back together again! Par-tay!<br />Book: Things are looking good<br />Book: They may even become a couple<br />Book: He told her he loves her!! *throws confetti*<br />Book: But hang on...<br />Book: Wait-<br />Book: And she's going to tell him she- OH WAIT HE'S LEAVING, sike!<br />Book: ACKNOWLEDGEMENTS (where the author will proceed to shower you with the number of dogs they have, a bunch of adjectives describing their editing staff and the name of their favourite chocolate brand).<br /><br />Dear authors - READERS HATE CLIFFHANGERS!<br /><br />I mean, have you ever met one reader that THANKED you for giving them a cliffhanger?! Cliffhangers are like smoking. Or parachuting without a parachute. They cause the following things:<br /> - Heart palpitations<br /> - Sobbing<br /> - Crying<br /> - Pain<br /> - Sniffling<br /> - Pain<br /> - Swooning<br /> - Incoherent screaming (e.g. "OH THE FEELS!", "WHY?!", "WHAT IS THIS?!")<br /> - Throwing of objects and people<br /> - Pain<br /> - More pain<br /> - Endless pain<br /> - NEVER ENDING PAIN GOOD GOD WHY DID YOU DO THIS I'M DYING MAKE IT STOP!<br /><br />So yep. I have finished my rant. You may now leave - wiser and stronger :D (And maybe slightly weirded out!)</span>
  <a data-text-id="1325018594501757609" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/236046056" />
    <a title="Katrina Passick Lumsden" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1964146-katrina-passick-lumsden"><img alt="Katrina Passick Lumsden" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1416959676p2/1964146.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/236046056?book_show_action=true">Nov 15, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katrina Passick Lumsden" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katrina Passick Lumsden" href="/user/show/1964146-katrina-passick-lumsden">Katrina Passick Lumsden</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer236046056" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11430125973469923176">So...mashed potatoes. That's what this book is. Mashed potatoes. Tastes kinda good, relatively harmless and easy to digest, but nothing spectacular. Sort of bland, but occasionally satisfies a particular craving. Mashed potatoes. <br/><br/>Yes. Not the real, red-skinned taters mashed potatoes, we're talking good old boxed taters. <br/><br/>Premise was good, but it was kind of slow. It seemed to take forever for Maggie and Caleb to see each other again, but once they did, it was like instant love....which just didn'</span>
  <span id="freeText11430125973469923176" style="display:none">So...mashed potatoes. That's what this book is. Mashed potatoes. Tastes kinda good, relatively harmless and easy to digest, but nothing spectacular. Sort of bland, but occasionally satisfies a particular craving. Mashed potatoes. <br /><br />Yes. Not the real, red-skinned taters mashed potatoes, we're talking good old boxed taters. <br /><br />Premise was good, but it was kind of slow. It seemed to take forever for Maggie and Caleb to see each other again, but once they did, it was like instant love....which just didn't settle well with me. I also generally dislike it when female authors try to speak through a male protagonist....it almost never comes across as genuine. Caleb's POV sounded suspiciously feminine and that made his macho persona a bit cheesy. <br /><br />I can see why a lot of teen girls love this, however. Ms. Elkeles isn't a half-bad writer and there are some good lessons to be learned. It's just that, when you get to be even my age (which is only 30), these particular issues seem almost unrealistically juvenile. <br /><br />Good for the teen set. Anyone over the age of 19 or 20, however, might find it a bit too grating.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11430125973469923176" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_97058601" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/97058601" />
    <a title=" Lady Jayne *~*The Beach Bandida*~*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1453659-lady-jayne-the-beach-bandida"><img alt=" Lady Jayne *~*The Beach Bandida*~*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1295034921p2/1453659.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/97058601?book_show_action=true">Apr 04, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" Lady Jayne *~*The Beach Bandida*~*" class="user" itemprop="url" name=" Lady Jayne *~*The Beach Bandida*~*" href="/user/show/1453659-lady-jayne-the-beach-bandida"> Lady Jayne *~*The Beach Bandida*~*</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">YA Romance readers</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to  Lady Jayne *~*The Beach Bandida*~* by: </span>
      My love of Perfect Chemistry by this author.
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1453659-lady-jayne-the-beach-bandida?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1453659-lady-jayne-the-beach-bandida?shelf=owned-read">owned-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1453659-lady-jayne-the-beach-bandida?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer97058601" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12512457265388107137">(4 Stars)<br/><br/>Loved this! Can't wait for the second book, Return to Paradise, coming out in September 2010, as the story is not over yet. Longer review to follow later.<br/>.................<br/><br/><i>Almost half a year later….my review...</i><br/><br/>(4.5 Stars)<br/><br/>I’m <i>finally</i> writing my review after my re-reading of <i>Leaving Paradise</i> just prior to reading the sequel, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7797874.Return_to_Paradise__Leaving_Paradise___2_' title='Return to Paradise (Leaving Paradise, #2) by Simone Elkeles' rel='nofollow noopener'>Return to Paradise</a>.<br/><br/>Earlier this year I read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4268157.Perfect_Chemistry__Perfect_Chemistry___1_' title='Perfect Chemistry (Perfect Chemistry, #1) by Simone Elkeles' rel='nofollow noopener'>Perfect Chemistry</a> by this author, and absolutely <b>LOVED</b> it and Alex and Brittany. Alex is one of my fave YA heroes! So sigh/</span>
  <span id="freeText12512457265388107137" style="display:none">(4 Stars)<br><br>Loved this! Can't wait for the second book, Return to Paradise, coming out in September 2010, as the story is not over yet. Longer review to follow later.<br>.................<br><br><i>Almost half a year later….my review...</i><br><br>(4.5 Stars)<br><br>I’m <i>finally</i> writing my review after my re-reading of <i>Leaving Paradise</i> just prior to reading the sequel, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7797874.Return_to_Paradise__Leaving_Paradise___2_" title="Return to Paradise (Leaving Paradise, #2) by Simone Elkeles" rel="nofollow noopener">Return to Paradise</a>.<br><br>Earlier this year I read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4268157.Perfect_Chemistry__Perfect_Chemistry___1_" title="Perfect Chemistry (Perfect Chemistry, #1) by Simone Elkeles" rel="nofollow noopener">Perfect Chemistry</a> by this author, and absolutely <b>LOVED</b> it and Alex and Brittany. Alex is one of my fave YA heroes! So sigh/swoon-sworthy.<br><br>While I enjoyed and loved Leaving Paradise and Caleb and Maggie, too, I didn’t love it quite much as Perfect Chemistry and hence the 4 Stars. Though, reading this the second time around and being thoroughly drawn in again, I am going to bump it up to 4.5 Stars, though recognising Ms Elkeles' growth as a writer in Perfect Chemistry. <br><br><i>Leaving Paradise</i> is the story of two teens whose lives (and that of their families) were both changed forever a result of a drunk driving hit-and-run accident. The story is told from Maggie’s and Caleb’s alternating first person point-of-views, giving us an intimate view into their thoughts and feelings.<br><br>Maggie Armstrong has spent the past year in hospitals and physical therapy as a result of the accident. She fears that she may walk with a limp for the rest of her life. Every time she looks at the ugly red scars etched across her left leg from the numerous surgeries, she is reminded of that painful night and how life just hasn’t been the same since. Her father has left, she lost not only her circle of friends but her best friend, can no longer play tennis, and her time away from school has left her feeling isolated and alone...like a freak.<br><br>Caleb Becker, Maggie’s neighbour, ex-best friend’s brother, and Maggie’s secret crush since her childhood, was convicted of Maggie’s hit-and-run and has spent the past year in juvenile detention. While he is happy to be free, he returns to Paradise to find his family in turmoil, and he realises that he can't just slip right back into his life again. <br><br><i>"It's hard keeping everything the same when the same things look and feel so different."</i> <br><br>What both Maggie and Caleb want is just to leave Paradise.<br><br>Yet, being neighbours, as well as other chance encounters, forces them to confront their grief and anger since that tragic night, and they end up finding love and solace in each other. This is a raw and touching story of two people struggling to forgive and trust and move on from a reckless accident, which scarred them both in different but profound ways. Their fears, frustrations and pain felt honest and real. And their romantic yet complicated love left me aching. What I wish I had known before I started it, though, was that Caleb and Maggie’s story did not end with this book.<br><br>Oh, and I just have to mention that I LOVE the cover!<br><br>Some of my fave quotes/scenes;<br><br><i>"Are you following me?" she asks, but doesn't meet my gaze. <br>"Yeah," I say. <br>"Why?" <br>I give her the only honest and true answer I have. "You're where I want to be." <br>....<br><br>"I look down at our knees, slightly touching. Jeans against jeans. Does she notice the heat transferring from her body to mine? Does she even realize what she's doing to me? I know, I know. I'm not a virgin and the slightest touch of a girl's knee is driving me insane. I don't even know what I'm feeling for Maggie, I just know that I'm <b>feeling.</b> It's something I've tried to avoid and deny until yesterday, when I held her in my arms while her tears spilled onto my shirt. <br><br>God, our knees touching isn't enough. I need more. <br><br>She's knotting her fingers together on her lap as if she doesn't know what to do with them. I want to touch her, but what if she pulls away like before? I've never been such a wuss with a girl in my life. <br><br>I bite my bottom lip as I slide my hand about millionth of a millimeter closer to her hand. <br><br>She doesn't seem fazed so I move closer. And closer. <br><br>When the tips of my fingers touch her wrist, she freezes. But she doesn't jerk her hand away. <b>God, her skin is so soft,</b> I think as my fingers trail a path from her wrist to her knuckles to her smooth, manicured nails. <br><br>I swear touching her like this is driving me nuts. It's more erotic, more intense than any other time with Kendra. I feel awkward and inexperienced as a freshman again. I look up. Everyone else is oblivious to the intensity of emotions running rampant in the back of the public bus. <br><br>When I look back down at my hand covering hers, I'm grateful she hasn't come to her senses and pulled away. As if she knows my thoughts, we both turn our hands at the same time so our hands are palm against palm...finger against finger. Her hand is dwarfed against mine. It makes her seem more delicate and petite than I'd realize. I feel a need to protect her and be her champion should she ever need one. <br><br>With a slight shift of my hand, I lace my fingers through hers. <br><br>I'm holding hands. With Maggie Armstrong.” *SIGHS*<br>....<br><br>“…the next time I kiss you it'll last a long, long time. And when we're done you're going to realize being turned on is not about experience." </i> *SHIVERS*<br><br><br>Okay…I’ve been hooked on <i>The Gates</i> lately so my current images may have slightly been coloured by that. ^_^<br><br><b>My Caleb (Colton Haynes):</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/603004.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379774935i/336433._SY540_.jpg" width="320" height="410" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>My Maggie (Skyler Samuels - but with light brown hair and hazel eyes):</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380333685i/693414._SX540_.jpg" width="385" height="280" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380333685i/693415.jpg" width="385" height="280" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><p>
  <br>

If any of these images are yours and you would like me to remove them, please let me know, and I will do so as soon as possible. If I can identify the copyright, I will do so.</i>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer425703965" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13711470340663891828">**2.5 stars**<br/><br/><b>I am totes not on the bandwagon for this book.</b><br/><br/>Was this book <i>bad</i>? No, not at all. I think this author has some talent and I liked the shifting POVs. The story actually seemed vaguely familiar to me but I liked the concept behind it. I would most definitely read more by this author in the future. <br/><br/>However, a few things about this book really rubbed me the wrong way.<br/><br/><b>1) I think that Maggie's reactions are totally unrealistic.</b> If a boy hit me with his car and PERMANENTLY MAIMED ME. I woul</span>
  <span id="freeText13711470340663891828" style="display:none">**2.5 stars**<br /><br /><b>I am totes not on the bandwagon for this book.</b><br /><br />Was this book <i>bad</i>? No, not at all. I think this author has some talent and I liked the shifting POVs. The story actually seemed vaguely familiar to me but I liked the concept behind it. I would most definitely read more by this author in the future. <br /><br />However, a few things about this book really rubbed me the wrong way.<br /><br /><b>1) I think that Maggie's reactions are totally unrealistic.</b> If a boy hit me with his car and PERMANENTLY MAIMED ME. I would be crazy, insane-style mad at him. I wanted angsty scenes full of "F-you!!!"s and "F you and your mother to the end of the world!!!" She should be downright vitriolic. Spitting poison at his face snake-style. Instead, Maggie barely calls Caleb on anything. She acts all meek and then falls back in love with him in a matter of days. <br /><br /><b>2) The "big twist."</b> Okay, this just irritated me. I think it was kind of a cop out and Caleb's behavior didn't really reflect that the twist ever happened. I would have expected a totally different attitude after finding out the "twist." Something about it didn't sit right.<br /><br /><b>3) The cliffhanger ending.</b> Need I say more???<br /><br /><b>4) The stereotypical teenage "scene".</b> So boring. So <i>done.</i><br /><br />Overall, this book didn't work for me like I hoped it would. Again, not awful but I probably won't remember it in a week. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13711470340663891828" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_134112680" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/134112680" />
    <a title="Lora" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4632071-lora"><img alt="Lora" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1305237530p2/4632071.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/134112680?book_show_action=true">Dec 08, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lora" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lora" href="/user/show/4632071-lora">Lora</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/7848548-leaving-paradise">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4632071-lora?shelf=g-ya-realistic">g-ya-realistic</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer134112680" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15407423309476464299">Before I reveal why I'm only giving this one 2.5 stars, let's go over what I liked:<br/><br/>The writing. I'd have to say that was my favorite part of this novel. Just like with Elkeles' <i>Perfect Chemistry</i> series, it was spectacular. She always knows how to depict teens as they <i>really</i> are. She doesn't choose to sugarcoat their more amorous feelings or leave out curse words to make her novels more "teen friendly." I love that because, for me, it's better to be realistic than to make prudes happy.<br/><br/>The charact</span>
  <span id="freeText15407423309476464299" style="display:none">Before I reveal why I'm only giving this one 2.5 stars, let's go over what I liked:<br /><br />The writing. I'd have to say that was my favorite part of this novel. Just like with Elkeles' <i>Perfect Chemistry</i> series, it was spectacular. She always knows how to depict teens as they <i>really</i> are. She doesn't choose to sugarcoat their more amorous feelings or leave out curse words to make her novels more "teen friendly." I love that because, for me, it's better to be realistic than to make prudes happy.<br /><br />The characters. I don't think that I felt as big of a connection as I would have liked. They were good, certainly better than a lot of characters I've read about, but not as good as with her other novels.<br /><br />Which brings me to the reason for my rating:<br />The pacing. Just didn't work for me. Everything just felt too rushed. Each chapter is very short, with each chapter switching POVs between Caleb and Maggie; this would have been fine if maybe the novel was fifty pages longer, but, unfortunately, it wasn't.<br /><br />Despite this, though, I still urge all who've not yet read this (I'm talking to you, Nic) to read it soon. Because, all in all, it was a very enjoyable read do to the writing, and the plot was very unique and refreshing.<br /><br />Bottom line, read it if you're a fan of Elkeles' writing.<br /><br />RATING: 2.5 stars.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15407423309476464299" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_78453786" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/78453786" />
    <a title="Kim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1594906-kim"><img alt="Kim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1252264728p2/1594906.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/78453786?book_show_action=true">Nov 20, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kim" href="/user/show/1594906-kim">Kim</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1594906-kim?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1594906-kim?shelf=read-in-2010">read-in-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1594906-kim?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer78453786" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6557168380248475439">Again, this is one of those books that leave me with a 'why didn't I read this sooner?' feeling.<br/><br/>I kept seeing this pop up on my flist and I enjoyed it <i>a lot</i>. <br/><br/>Usually, when I read about female characters, my thoughts go from 'why can't I be more like her' to 'for the love of god, please somebody, slap her!' but this time I recognized something of myself in Maggie.<br/><br/>The part where Caleb makes her play tennis again, and she secretly loves it but doesn't want to admit it, that's exactly how I am. Tryi</span>
  <span id="freeText6557168380248475439" style="display:none">Again, this is one of those books that leave me with a 'why didn't I read this sooner?' feeling.<br /><br />I kept seeing this pop up on my flist and I enjoyed it <i>a lot</i>. <br /><br />Usually, when I read about female characters, my thoughts go from 'why can't I be more like her' to 'for the love of god, please somebody, slap her!' but this time I recognized something of myself in Maggie.<br /><br />The part where Caleb makes her play tennis again, and she secretly loves it but doesn't want to admit it, that's exactly how I am. Trying (new) things, getting over myself and my fears... that's about as scary as it gets for me. I'd wish I'd meet the person who can pull me over all my obstacles. <br /><br />Caleb's decision sucks. I was torn between wanting to smack Leah around and feeling sorry for her. She needs to man up and face the music. Her brother went to jail for christ's sake. Stop being so selfish. Kendra is the kind of girl I would beat up. A lot. Six words out of her mouth and my fist would be in it. And to all the parents in this book, I suggest putting <a href="http://www.coverbrowser.com/image/books-about-parenting/391-1.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">this little gem</a> on your Christmas lists.<br /><br />Sequel, where are you?</span>
  <a data-text-id="6557168380248475439" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2593275536" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2593275536" />
    <a title=" Amelia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32236773-amelia"><img alt=" Amelia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593283361p2/32236773.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2593275536?book_show_action=true">Jan 08, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" Amelia" class="user" itemprop="url" name=" Amelia" href="/user/show/32236773-amelia"> Amelia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32236773-amelia?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32236773-amelia?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32236773-amelia?shelf=2000-2009">2000-2009</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2593275536" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2243038404213552887">*FULL OF SPOILERS AFTER THE FIRST PARAGRAPH, BEWARE* <br/><br/>My first issue with this book was <b> Caleb </b>. He was so annoying and I loathed every aspect of him. He just let everyone tell him what to do, it's like he couldn't think for himself. Even if he disagreed with someone or didn't want to do something, he'd just accept it and do whatever it is they told him to do, because he feels it's just easier to do that than to argue - or as we normal people say - give your opinion and stand up for yourself. <br/><br/>" '</span>
  <span id="freeText2243038404213552887" style="display:none">*FULL OF SPOILERS AFTER THE FIRST PARAGRAPH, BEWARE* <br><br>My first issue with this book was <b> Caleb </b>. He was so annoying and I loathed every aspect of him. He just let everyone tell him what to do, it's like he couldn't think for himself. Even if he disagreed with someone or didn't want to do something, he'd just accept it and do whatever it is they told him to do, because he feels it's just easier to do that than to argue - or as we normal people say - give your opinion and stand up for yourself. <br><br>" 'That's cool,' because, well, what else can I say? "<br><br>Maybe YOUR OPINION YOU DUMBASS<br><br>Not only that, but he's also kind of a douchebag. So he gets back from jail, hangs out with his ex (not talking or doing anything important, just making out because that's obviously the only thing they can do) then falls for Maggie - of course - but even though he's all "in love" with Maggie and "can't stop thinking about her" he still hooks up with his ex AGAIN and hopes Maggie doesn't see them -.- <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1546989531ra/26887349.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And while we're talking about his ex...Her name is Kendra and she is the typical perfect-blonde-popular-mean-girl that likes to make everyone miserable. She also "makes" Caleb sleep with her because she can and because, as I already said, he just can't say no to anyone, especially to a pretty girl with full lips and large breasts...Yes, he mentions this a couple of times.<br><br>Maggie is no better. She's literally doing nothing for half of the book and then suddenly makes an amazing recovery because she had a boyfriend. Here's basically what the plot looks like for Maggie: she feels sorry for herself 90% of the time, she does nothing and talks to no one at school and still wonders why she has no friends and why everyone thinks she's weird. She also talks a lot about how she HATES Caleb and how nothing is the same ever since he hit her and she hopes she'll never see him again...Until she sees him. It took her maybe a week after he got back to start crushing on him AGAIN. That's right, of course Caleb is her ex BFFs brother, so naturally, she had a crush on him since forever. Anyways, as I said, a few days have passed and what else is there to do than to fall hard for the guy who ran over you with his car? They have several make-out sessions, he saves her from some bullies blah blah blah Then we get to maybe 80% of the book and I just knew it -they break up. There's always the break up towards the end before they can dramatically get back together -.- <br><br>Now at that point, I'm already bored and know exactly what's going to happen, but what I don't expect is another ridiculous thing that just adds to the list of things that are badly done in this book -&gt; the miraculous recovery Maggie makes after she dumps him. If there's one thing I hate in books that deal with health problems, it's when the MC or whoever, makes A FULL RECOVERY in the span of like 2 days BECAUSE OF A LOVE INTEREST. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1505737906ra/23955340.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Relationships are a HUGE part of recovery, but they don't work like this. Basically what happens is this: Declan does something stupid, like always, Maggie breaks up with him, decides she's suddenly strong and can do anything she wants in like 5 minutes - in the same day she finally does what she hasn't been able to do for a whole year: she stands up to her bullies, decides she won't run away to Spain, stops hiding her scars and becomes comfortable in her own skin and basically becomes a different person. All of this things are great and of course I wanted that for her - but this is just unrealistic. At least it was for me.<br><br>Moving on. Maggie also likes to talk A LOT about Kendra (and other girls), mostly like this:<br><br>"How could I ever have thought I could compete with perfect Kendra Greene?"<br><br>"God, they look so...perfect."<br><br>She's always comparing herself with them and making a pity party every 10 seconds. We get it, you're no longer part of the popular crowd. Get over it.<br><br>Then there's the completely unnecessary character death that's only there so it could add to the sadness and drama. It's just a tool to make the reader more emotional but it failed to do so with me. I felt absolutely nothing because it was so obvious it was just a plot device and a way to make the MCs get closer.<br><br>Now we get to the ending....As I already guessed 10% in, Caleb wasn't actually the one who hit Maggie and ran away, it was his twin sister Leah and Maggie's BFF. Not only was that so predictable, it was also done poorly. In the very last chapter, Maggie suddenly remembers the accident and who was driving. She goes on to visit Caleb, who leaves because why not create additional drama and make the reader read the sequel, she then meets up with Leah. Leah tries to tell her it was her fault (even though she was basically THE WORST throughout the book and did nothing to help her brother or her BFF) but Maggie says something like "I already know, it doesn't matter, let's go get some pie :)" LIKE WHAT EVEN. She literally found out 3 seconds ago that her BFF lied to her for MONTHS knowing she was angry at her brother and generally sad, and she just forgave her like it was nothing....<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1518179239ra/25030813.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>EXCUSE ME. I love my BFF and all that, but if I found out that it was in fact her who ran over me and THEN LEFT ME THERE ON THE ROAD AND DID NOTHING EXCEPT LIE AND FRAME SOMEONE ELSE...I'd be a tad angry. I'm all for forgiveness, but this? This is not...normal. She LITERALLY forgave her the same day, I'm not exaggerating, that's what happened. Anyways, I'm so done with this that I lowered the rating from 2.5 to 2 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2243038404213552887" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_123595217" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/123595217" />
    <a title="Buggy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3099666-buggy"><img alt="Buggy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1289702969p2/3099666.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/123595217?book_show_action=true">Sep 26, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Buggy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Buggy" href="/user/show/3099666-buggy">Buggy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3099666-buggy?shelf=scars-r-sexy">scars-r-sexy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3099666-buggy?shelf=shelf-11">shelf-11</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3099666-buggy?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3099666-buggy?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer123595217" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4597750186736508503">Opening Line: <i>"I'd been waiting a year for this moment"</i><br/><br/>4.5~ I don’t generally read much YA stuff but Caleb and Maggie’s forbidden coming of age romance got to me and I found myself quite wrapped up in all their teenaged angst. I guess it was the unique story idea that first piqued my interest; that of a romance developing between the offender and his victim was too good to pass up. And once you get into it the reasoning’s as to why they get together it felt realistic. I mean they‘ve both been aw</span>
  <span id="freeText4597750186736508503" style="display:none">Opening Line: <i>"I'd been waiting a year for this moment"</i><br /><br />4.5~ I don’t generally read much YA stuff but Caleb and Maggie’s forbidden coming of age romance got to me and I found myself quite wrapped up in all their teenaged angst. I guess it was the unique story idea that first piqued my interest; that of a romance developing between the offender and his victim was too good to pass up. And once you get into it the reasoning’s as to why they get together it felt realistic. I mean they‘ve both been away for a year and things have changed, they‘ve changed and none of their friends “get” them anymore. Throw in some majorly screwed up family members, a big secret and super cool old lady and you’ve got yourselves a great story.<br /> <br />Told with alternating POV’s for each chapter, this was a fast read and I enjoyed getting into both Maggie and Caleb’s heads, seeing what each of them thought of the same situation. We begin with our hero Caleb being released from jail. He’s just spent a year locked up in juvenile detention for hitting a girl with his car while drunk and then leaving the scene. He’s paid his dues though and is no longer the carefree popular teen that went away. All he wants now is to go home and resume his life, -well that and turn back time. With getting released comes a few rules though, like 150 hours of community service, meeting with a transition counsellor and staying out of trouble. It’s all easier said then done.<br /><br />Switching to Maggie we join her in physical therapy exercising her shattered leg and preparing to go back to school. The only thing that gets her through the day now is her scholarship to Spain. It seems since the accident she’s no longer one of the popular kids, they all think she’s a freak and Maggie can’t wait to get out of this town and away from their whispers and stares. <br /><br />Through circumstance Maggie takes a job as a companion for old Mrs Reynolds (who turned out to be one of my favourite characters) Coincidentally she’s also just hired Caleb through his community service. I guess in a town as small as Paradise they should have expected to run into each other but what neither had expected was that it would only be the other that could truly understand what they’re going through. Caleb’s family is really messed up; his sister is a Goth ghost, his mother acts like nothing has happened and his father is just gone. And then there's his ex-girlfriend, beautiful, seductive and full of poison. Maggie’s days of playing tennis are over and her overprotective Mum (eek) is dating her boss. What an embarrassment.<br /><br />Bound together by the tragedy yet forbidden by their parents and a court order to be together a tentative friendship begins, quickly developing into something neither of them had expected or can stop. A bittersweet, moving love story, now I only wish I had <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7797874.Return_to_Paradise__Leaving_Paradise___2_" title="Return to Paradise (Leaving Paradise, #2) by Simone Elkeles" rel="nofollow noopener">Return to Paradise</a> because the ending here leaves you hanging. I’ll definitely be reading more from Simone Elkeles. Cheers </span>
  <a data-text-id="4597750186736508503" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_160448909" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/160448909" />
    <a title="Donna {Book Passion For Life}" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3024878-donna-book-passion-for-life"><img alt="Donna {Book Passion For Life}" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1563622982p2/3024878.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/160448909?book_show_action=true">Apr 11, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Donna {Book Passion For Life}" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Donna {Book Passion For Life}" href="/user/show/3024878-donna-book-passion-for-life">Donna {Book Passion For Life}</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3024878-donna-book-passion-for-life?shelf=ya-contemporary-romance">ya-contemporary-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer160448909" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer754173577003916551">Posted on: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://bookpassionforlife.blogspot.com/'>http://bookpassionforlife.blogspot.com/</a><br/><br/>After reading Simone Elkeles Perfect Chemistry series, I've been itching to find something just as good. And while I have read a few books that have been really good, nothing had been better than Perfect Chemistry. Well……that is until Leaving Paradise completely surpassed all my expectations and blew me completely away! <br/><br/>Both Maggie Armstrong & Caleb Becker's lives changed one fateful night after Caleb accidently ran over Maggie while drunk drivin</span>
  <span id="freeText754173577003916551" style="display:none">Posted on: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://bookpassionforlife.blogspot.com/">http://bookpassionforlife.blogspot.com/</a><br /><br />After reading Simone Elkeles Perfect Chemistry series, I've been itching to find something just as good. And while I have read a few books that have been really good, nothing had been better than Perfect Chemistry. Well……that is until Leaving Paradise completely surpassed all my expectations and blew me completely away! <br /><br />Both Maggie Armstrong &amp; Caleb Becker's lives changed one fateful night after Caleb accidently ran over Maggie while drunk driving. While leaving Maggie for dead and with a permanent limp for life, Caleb has spent the last year in a juvenile jail. When Caleb is finally released, he and Maggie both try to move on with their lives but it’s hard when fate seems to have other plans for them……leaving them to both fighting their attraction for one another. <br /><br />When I started reading this book, admittedly I thought it was a little slow to start off with….but….don’t let that put you off from reading it. While reading it, I realised that we were slowly starting to find out how both, Caleb and Maggie felt about that fateful night. Not only did we find out what they felt but also that they both have different views of it too. With the story alternating from different point of views, you really get inside these characters head and really see them for who they really are. I honestly love two different views and I wish all books would do it. <br /><br />Caleb and Maggie were both great characters. Yes, they have a lot baggage but it’s nothing they can’t work through. While the chemistry between them is so undeniable, I honestly sat on the edge of my seat while reading it. The suspense, the heat and attraction is just skimming on top of the surface and you’re just waiting for it to burst out. Simone Elkeles has done a fantastic job while she tells a hard story bringing together the two people that it has affected the most. She also writes raw, passionate and intense scenes that leave the readers wanting more and more. Oh…..and when you think you know the full story.....wham! A massive shocker is thrown into the story.....that I for one, WAS NOT expecting! Wow! Just wow! <br /><br />Overall….Leaving Paradise left me needing to find out more about our characters that I’m headed for book two straight away. Read this book guys…I promise you won’t be disappointed. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="754173577003916551" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_203077089" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/203077089" />
    <a title="Thomas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2018505-thomas"><img alt="Thomas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567953607p2/2018505.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/203077089?book_show_action=true">Aug 28, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Thomas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Thomas" href="/user/show/2018505-thomas">Thomas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer203077089" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7006221024937855372">3.5 stars.<br/><br/>Caleb Becker and Maggie Armstrong have spent the last year imprisoned. Caleb, imprisoned in juvenile detention for hitting Maggie while driving under the influence, and Maggie, imprisoned by physical therapy sessions for her damaged left leg that leaves her with a limp. When the two are forced together again after that one fateful night, how will they deal with the guilt and anxiety of trusting the person who's ruined ruined them forever?<br/><br/><i>Leaving Paradise</i> possesses an interesting premis</span>
  <span id="freeText7006221024937855372" style="display:none">3.5 stars.<br /><br />Caleb Becker and Maggie Armstrong have spent the last year imprisoned. Caleb, imprisoned in juvenile detention for hitting Maggie while driving under the influence, and Maggie, imprisoned by physical therapy sessions for her damaged left leg that leaves her with a limp. When the two are forced together again after that one fateful night, how will they deal with the guilt and anxiety of trusting the person who's ruined ruined them forever?<br /><br /><i>Leaving Paradise</i> possesses an interesting premise, but Elkeles didn't take the story to its highest potential. Questions of betrayal, forgiveness, and trust are explored, though not to the depth that would have made this book amazing. Caleb and Maggie were good characters, yet they lacked the emotional complexity to make their struggles entirely believable.<br /><br />The pacing of the plot also left something to be desired - it seemed rushed and too many things fell into place at exactly the right moment. The ending was clearly crafted to leave room for a sequel, which isn't necessarily a bad thing but not a good thing either.<br /><br />Similar to her books <i>Perfect Chemistry</i> and <i>Rules of Attraction</i> Elkeles's writing flows without a hitch. However, I did notice the occasional grammar mistake or typo that easily could have been caught by a better editor.<br /><br />Overall, if you're a fan of Simone Elkeles I would recommend reading this book. I'm still debating myself whether to read the second book, <i>Return to Paradise</i>.<br /><br />*cross-posted from my blog, <a href="http://thequietvoice18.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">the quiet voice</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7006221024937855372" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/200912009?book_show_action=true">Aug 21, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/10490380-leaving-paradise">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer16474529197095738589">Lots of lessons to be learned in this book. I liked the alternating points-of-view between Maggie and Caleb. My heart ached for both of them and all that they had lost. Maggie's struggle with her debilitating injury and the stares and teasing she was victim of, was just so wrong!! People just made fun of her and didn't understand the physical pain Maggie was suffering from was almost more than she could bear. Then to have to listen to the snickering and rude comments...it just made me want to sm</span>
  <span id="freeText16474529197095738589" style="display:none">Lots of lessons to be learned in this book. I liked the alternating points-of-view between Maggie and Caleb. My heart ached for both of them and all that they had lost. Maggie's struggle with her debilitating injury and the stares and teasing she was victim of, was just so wrong!! People just made fun of her and didn't understand the physical pain Maggie was suffering from was almost more than she could bear. Then to have to listen to the snickering and rude comments...it just made me want to smack someone. Caleb's parents were the so un-supportive and his sister needed a good shaking to WAKE HER UP!! I can't imagine being his age and coming home to nothing but criticism from his own mother and father after the living hell he went through. They never really welcomed him back. <br /><br />I enjoyed the connection that Caleb and Maggie found with one another and thought their relationship was very sweet. If only everything else and everyone else...namely Kendra, couldn't stand her...didn't get in the way. One of my favorite characters was the charming, blunt, but very wise Mrs. Reynolds. The time they spent with her was some of the best in the book. The book had the potential to wrap up and go no further, but it seems that Caleb and Maggie’s story was not meant to come to a conclusion just yet. So, it’s on to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7797874.Return_to_Paradise__Leaving_Paradise___2_" title="Return to Paradise (Leaving Paradise, #2) by Simone Elkeles" rel="nofollow noopener">Return to Paradise</a> to see how the story plays out! <br /></span>

<div id="review_270385065" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/270385065" />
    <a title="Annie Brewer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5315988-annie-brewer"><img alt="Annie Brewer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442496062p2/5315988.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/270385065?book_show_action=true">Jan 31, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Annie Brewer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Annie Brewer" href="/user/show/5315988-annie-brewer">Annie Brewer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">everyone who loves romance</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Annie by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/3161105-maida---v--">Maida»-(¯`v´¯)-»</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5315988-annie-brewer?shelf=absolutely-amazingly-awesome">absolutely-amazingly-awesome</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5315988-annie-brewer?shelf=favorite">favorite</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5315988-annie-brewer?shelf=nook-books">nook-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5315988-annie-brewer?shelf=irresistable-hot-guys">irresistable-hot-guys</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5315988-annie-brewer?shelf=favorite-authors">favorite-authors</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer270385065" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7749880521461690239">LOVE LOVE LOVE this book!!!!!! Absolutely amazing! Review to come!!<br/><br/><br/><br/><br/>Okay, um I am not sure where to start. Well, let me start by saying Simone Elkeles has become a favorite author because of this book. I bought it on my nook cause it was cheap plus I loved the cover plus I have heard great things about it and my friend told me how amazing it is. And Maida, you were so right on!!!! This book was just....just. It just was. The romance, the story line, the characters, all of it was superb at its fin</span>
  <span id="freeText7749880521461690239" style="display:none">LOVE LOVE LOVE this book!!!!!! Absolutely amazing! Review to come!!<br /><br /><br /><br /><br />Okay, um I am not sure where to start. Well, let me start by saying Simone Elkeles has become a favorite author because of this book. I bought it on my nook cause it was cheap plus I loved the cover plus I have heard great things about it and my friend told me how amazing it is. And Maida, you were so right on!!!! This book was just....just. It just was. The romance, the story line, the characters, all of it was superb at its finest. I am glad I read it first, I know everyone wants me to read the Perfect Chemistry books and believe me I will get to them. This was my first Elkeles book to read and she had me captivated from the start! I will be reading every book she ever wrote or writes for sure! YAY! Okay so let's get on with this review shall we?<br /><br /><br />So Maggie Armstrong and Caleb Becker have known each other since they were kids and they have been neighbors as well. Maggies is best friends with Leah, Caleb's twin sister....until the night that changed everything. And boy was it a drastic change. While Caleb is the typical HOT popular God that girls swoon over and guys hate but still look up to, Maggie is just mediocre until her and Leah slide into the popular crowd. At a party one night, things get a little heated and Caleb gets drunk fighting with Maggie about his current girlfriend Kendra. Drunk and angry, Caleb hits Maggie with his car going home but doesn't check on her. But what really happened the night of the party? Only a couple of people know the truth, and it is a complete surprise. One thing's for sure, Maggie never walks the same again since she broke her leg-even surgeries wont fix it. So to avoid the embarrassment and humiliation of social suicide, Maggie is homeschooled the year of her junior year. <br /><br />Meanwhile, Caleb is thrown in jail on charges for drunk driving and a hit and run. He spends almost a year in there, paying his dues and gets of with community service. Going back to Paradise(his hometown), he finds that the life he left behind is the life that will never be repaired upon returning. His mother wont touch him, his father acts oblivious and fakes happiness eventhough their family has gone to shit, oh yea and Leah has become gothic ghost. He realizes nothing will be the same no matter how hard he tries. Going back to school is even different, everyone looks at him like an ex-con and though that might be true, there are secrets that noone knows about but he is not about to spill it and rumors float around about what went on while he was in jail. Eventually, Maggie and Caleb come face to face after a year and as awkward and ridiculous as it is, they find that they are the only people who understand what really happend and what it's like to be a popular turned outsider/ They tried to avoid each other, but their attraction and chemistry is too intense to ignore......can they fight it or will it destroy them forever?<br /><br />OKAY, so sorry that was quite long....I couldn't stop the words from flowing right out of me. My thoughts are this: I loved every bit of this story. There are some sad parts, some happy, some confusing, and definitely some surprising twists!! It was an emotional roller coaster and the ending was not what I was hoping for however, it was well developed and I know it will work out in the end in the next book. The book was written from both POV's, which everyone that knows me knows I love the guy's perspetive!! I loved Caleb even more because I got to see what he was going through despite the circumstances. I felt his emotions, his anger, fear, love, joy, betrayal, pain-and I wanted to hug him and tell him I was here(though it's not like he can hear me, he's a freaking fictional character)!!!! Dammit!!! But still, he was my favorite of them all. Once you read this, you will understand why I am not calling him a prick for hitting his friend and running off. Okay I will stop babbling about him. Love you Caleb!!!! &lt;3<br /><br />I still enjoyed the story from Maggie's view too. She was a caring, strong, level headed heroine and though she appeared weak at times, she still managed to captivate me. She went through a lot as Caleb did. This story really deals with real life issues and Elkeles did a great job weaving both POV's together to make it flow very smoothly. It was never choppy in anyway. <br /><br />Characters:<br /><br />I loved the dynami of each character, though I will say, I hated Kendra. She was your typical snotty bicth who I wanted punch her face in to her a lesson. She irked me the whole way and I swear I was angry in every scene with her. I liked Drew, who was Caleb's friend...he was funny and amuzed the hell outta me eventhough he was an ass at times. I didn't like Maggie's mom that much or either of Caleb's parents. I hope they shape up in the next one, if they are even in it. Leah had a small role so I can't say whether I liked her or not cause it would give away some important things. But one of my favorite characters was Mrs. Reynolds, an old lady who helped both Caleb and Maggie realize the importance in life. She was a huge part of their transformation and was the best influence they could have asked for. I admired her, she was so generous and kind. I think everyone will fall in love with her!! I also liked Damon, Caleb's transition coach who gave him a chance when no one else would have. He totally rocked my socks off!!!<br /><br />Honestly, I didn't see anything bad about this book!!! It was absolutely perfect the way it was!!! I can't wait to get into the sequel!!!! I know I will be a blubbering mess, I love happy endings and I have a good feeling about it! I definitely recommend this book to all with a love for sappy romances!! GO GET YOU A COPY!!!! You won't regret it!!!!<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7749880521461690239" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_64650477" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/64650477" />
    <a title="Arlene" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1746727-arlene"><img alt="Arlene" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1347048609p2/1746727.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/64650477?book_show_action=true">Jul 23, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Arlene" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Arlene" href="/user/show/1746727-arlene">Arlene</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781417783939" href="/book/show/2309032.Leaving_Paradise">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=read-2009">read-2009</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1746727-arlene?shelf=ya-contemporary">ya-contemporary</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer64650477" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17983589116638499752">Leaving Paradise by Simone Elkeles is such a great read! It’s the kind of book you pick up, keep turning the pages, and before you know it; you’re done with the story. I really enjoyed the format of the book and how the POV alternates between the two main characters.<br/> <br/>The author did a great job of developing both Caleb and Maggie’s character that you immediately come to care for both of them regardless of their opposing circumstance. It’s a unique storyline with a sad ending that will have most p</span>
  <span id="freeText17983589116638499752" style="display:none">Leaving Paradise by Simone Elkeles is such a great read! It’s the kind of book you pick up, keep turning the pages, and before you know it; you’re done with the story. I really enjoyed the format of the book and how the POV alternates between the two main characters.<br /> <br />The author did a great job of developing both Caleb and Maggie’s character that you immediately come to care for both of them regardless of their opposing circumstance. It’s a unique storyline with a sad ending that will have most people tearing up. <br /> <br />I wasn’t 100% happy with the ending, but once I thought about it, I realized it’s a more realistic ending rather than the HEA most books attempt to deliver. However, I was so hooked by the story that I did some research on it, and it sounds like there will be a sequel to this book. Lately, I’ve been boo’ing sequels, but reading Leaving Paradise has made me an instant fan of Simone Elkeles, so I look forward to book two in this series.<br /><br />About the story… Maggie Armstrong is a senior in high school returning after a year in the hospital and subsequent physical therapy as a result of being hit by a car that left her scarred and damaged both physically and emotionally. Upon her return, she must face her fellow students, who show little compassion for her circumstance and go so far as to ridicule her on her limp, which was a result of her accident. Even more challenging, she encounters Caleb Baker, who’s recently completed a year in the juvenile detention center after being accused of getting behind the wheel while intoxicated and changing Maggie’s life forever. These two teenagers both face emotional hardships in trying to achieve some semblance in their life and ultimately find solace in the most unlikely candidates… each other.<br /><br />There were tender moments that had me re-reading some passages, and the dialog was engaging and enjoyable. About three quarters of the way through, a reveal came about that surprised me and in a small sense, I found it unnecessary to the story. However, it didn’t take away from how I felt about Caleb and Maggie, and I rooted for them all the way through. I can’t wait for the sequel.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17983589116638499752" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_161639157" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/161639157" />
    <a title="Beatrice Masaluñga" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4590441-beatrice-masalu-ga"><img alt="Beatrice Masaluñga" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603719912p2/4590441.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/161639157?book_show_action=true">Apr 17, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beatrice Masaluñga" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beatrice Masaluñga" href="/user/show/4590441-beatrice-masalu-ga">Beatrice Masaluñga</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4590441-beatrice-masalu-ga?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4590441-beatrice-masalu-ga?shelf=favorite-books">favorite-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4590441-beatrice-masalu-ga?shelf=owned">owned</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer161639157" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4491925216125942768">It has been two or 3 years since I've read anything by <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/274533.Simone_Elkeles' title='Simone Elkeles' rel='nofollow noopener'>Simone Elkeles</a>. I still remember reading <i>
  <b>Perfect Chemistry</b>
</i> trilogy, which I absolutely love. I'm so glad that I've read another novel of hers, giving me this jittery and sad feeling. If you haven't read that trilogy, GO READ IT. Especially, if you love <i>Pushing the Limits</i> by <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4575371.Katie_McGarry' title='Katie McGarry' rel='nofollow noopener'>Katie McGarry</a>.<br/><br/><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>What happens when the person who damaged you for life... becomes the person you trust the most?</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br/><br/><i>Leaving Paradise</i> is an emotional roller coast</span>
  <span id="freeText4491925216125942768" style="display:none">It has been two or 3 years since I've read anything by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/274533.Simone_Elkeles" title="Simone Elkeles" rel="nofollow noopener">Simone Elkeles</a>. I still remember reading <i>
  <b>Perfect Chemistry</b>
</i> trilogy, which I absolutely love. I'm so glad that I've read another novel of hers, giving me this jittery and sad feeling. If you haven't read that trilogy, GO READ IT. Especially, if you love <i>Pushing the Limits</i> by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4575371.Katie_McGarry" title="Katie McGarry" rel="nofollow noopener">Katie McGarry</a>.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>What happens when the person who damaged you for life... becomes the person you trust the most?</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br /><br /><i>Leaving Paradise</i> is an emotional roller coaster read. There are moments of sadness, joy and love. Likely, it centers more on <u>forgiveness and recovery from a downfall</u>. This book has an alternating point of view between Caleb Becker and Maggie Armstrong. I love how the story is elaborated so that we get to know more about their life and struggles.<br /><br />Caleb spent his past year in prison/juvenile detention because of being drunk and hit his neighbor, Maggie Armstrong which changed both their lives and relationships with other people. These characters are damaged and vulnerable. Maggie's future has changed as she suffered with injuries that will forever leave a mark on her skin and undergone physical therapies for her leg because of a limp. Caleb's reputation as an ex-convict and earning not-so-good impressions.<br /><br /><b>What's good about it? </b> throughout the story,there are <u>character developments</u>. It's <u>beautifully written</u> though it took me a while to get into the story. I absolutely love love love the characters and the little twist. I'm not going to mention it here because I don't want to ruin some reading moments. <br /><br />Overall, I love it and I recommend this one. The last part of the story just... oh my dear. I need the next book. ASAP</span>
  <a data-text-id="4491925216125942768" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9133245553046089211">Street corner TBR Challenge<br/>August pick #4 per Flannery.<br/><br/><br/>Ahh, This was one of those books I just couldn't put down. I was reading it every spare second I had. I didn't know if Elkeles was going to be able to pull off anything as awesome as "perfect chemistry", but she definitely brought her A-game with this book. Although, it just sort of abruptly ended....<br/><br/>Spoilers:<br/>I hate that ending. I want the goo-goo, happy ending. This one was sad!   <span id="freeText9133245553046089211" style="display:none">Street corner TBR Challenge<br />August pick #4 per Flannery.<br /><br /><br />Ahh, This was one of those books I just couldn't put down. I was reading it every spare second I had. I didn't know if Elkeles was going to be able to pull off anything as awesome as "perfect chemistry", but she definitely brought her A-game with this book. Although, it just sort of abruptly ended....<br /><br />Spoilers:<br />I hate that ending. I want the goo-goo, happy ending. This one was sad! I hope there is some reconnecting in book #2. <br />Maggie, at first got under my skin. The way she was handling the accident was whiney and childish... but then I thought to myself, how would you have really reacted in High School if it happened to you??!?! Probably the same way, so it was realistic. She was angry and had a right to be. But, since we got to read inside Caleb's head it made me root for him. He really is a great guy- even if everyone in town thinks he is terrible. The way he is taking the blame for Leah just blows my mind. That is some sibling love. I am very glad that in the end atleast Leah and Maggie are working out their problems instead of running away. <br /><br />3.5 stars.... if you liked her other books, I believe you will be into this one as well. </span>
