<div id="review_198274977" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/198274977" />
    <a title="Emily" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2245895-emily"><img alt="Emily" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1341463199p2/2245895.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/198274977?book_show_action=true">Aug 14, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily" href="/user/show/2245895-emily">Emily</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer198274977" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3246364335452954583">Leaving Paradise is my very first Elkeles novel (I was an Elkeles virgin o.0). I'd read mixed reviews from my GR friends but most of her books have high average ratings so I was keen to see what the fuss was about. <br/><br/>As you can see from my measly 2 stars, I didn't <i>love</i> it. But I definitely didn't hate it either. I don't regret paying (something ridiculous like a dollar...) for it on my Kindle. Would I pay much more than that? I don't know. Probably not.<br/><br/>Let's get the ugly stuff out of the way first</span>
  <span id="freeText3246364335452954583" style="display:none">Leaving Paradise is my very first Elkeles novel (I was an Elkeles virgin o.0). I'd read mixed reviews from my GR friends but most of her books have high average ratings so I was keen to see what the fuss was about. <br /><br />As you can see from my measly 2 stars, I didn't <i>love</i> it. But I definitely didn't hate it either. I don't regret paying (something ridiculous like a dollar...) for it on my Kindle. Would I pay much more than that? I don't know. Probably not.<br /><br />Let's get the ugly stuff out of the way first: I was bored, I didn't connect with the characters and the writing felt stiff and unconvincing. Oh and sometimes it felt like an episode of The Bold and the Beautiful. (FYI, not a good thing for me.)<br /><br />Phew, now that's over I'm just going to tell you what I DID like, because I enjoy doing that so much more. I liked Maggie and Caleb. No, I didn't connect with them. And the jail stuff felt so contrived. But they didn't make me throw my book in frustration or anything like that. <br /><br />I kept reading till the end because I wanted some kind of satisfaction about Maggie and Caleb's relationship. I didn't end up getting it. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The "Let's go get pie" thing seemed so weird to me. Because I'm Aussie, pie makes me think meat pie (though obviously that's not what they meant) and it just confused me. Is that the moral of the story? Pie fixes all? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I also liked the premise. Girl likes guy, guy hits girl with car. But they're attracted to each other anyway. The premise was strong, but fell short in the delivery. <br /><br />It's one of those books that I sort of liked while I was reading it but, ultimately, it's forgettable. One of those books that ends with me thinking, "Well, at least that's another book read for my Goodreads challenge..." <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3246364335452954583" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_174775024" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/174775024" />
    <a title="Carla *Jen7waters*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3288963-carla-jen7waters"><img alt="Carla *Jen7waters*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594777797p2/3288963.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/174775024?book_show_action=true">Jun 08, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carla *Jen7waters*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carla *Jen7waters*" href="/user/show/3288963-carla-jen7waters">Carla *Jen7waters*</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/10490380-leaving-paradise">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3288963-carla-jen7waters?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3288963-carla-jen7waters?shelf=heroine-physically-challenged">heroine-physically-challenged</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3288963-carla-jen7waters?shelf=heroine-scarred">heroine-scarred</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3288963-carla-jen7waters?shelf=hero-i-wanna-slap">hero-i-wanna-slap</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3288963-carla-jen7waters?shelf=2015-read">2015-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3288963-carla-jen7waters?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3288963-carla-jen7waters?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer174775024" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8354651540487282273">I didn't hate this book, and the 1 star rating seems a bit harsh even for me, but so many things about this story bothered the hell out of me that I honestly cannot make myself click on that second star.<br/><br/>So the story is about this boy, Caleb, who hit his next door neighbor, Maggie, with a car while drunk driving, fled the scene, and went to jail for a year for it. Maggie survived but ended up with a permanently injured, scarred leg and a severe limp. The book starts when Caleb gets out of jail an</span>
  <span id="freeText8354651540487282273" style="display:none">I didn't hate this book, and the 1 star rating seems a bit harsh even for me, but so many things about this story bothered the hell out of me that I honestly cannot make myself click on that second star.<br /><br />So the story is about this boy, Caleb, who hit his next door neighbor, Maggie, with a car while drunk driving, fled the scene, and went to jail for a year for it. Maggie survived but ended up with a permanently injured, scarred leg and a severe limp. The book starts when Caleb gets out of jail and goes home, hopefully to get his life back on track, but everyone he knows, family, friends, ex-girlfriend, only see him and treat him like some kind of circus freak attraction dangerous ex-con. And then there's Maggie, who will not forgive him for the accident, and whom he has to work with in order to complete his sentence by doing community service.<br /><br />I never really connected with the characters, Caleb is kind of an asshole, constantly shaming his sister because she dresses in all black, makeup included, and he doesn't like it. I also hated the way he thought about Maggie for a big part of the story, like it was her fault that he went to jail, like her injured leg and scars were nothing compared to his own problems and the time he spent locked up. He never, not even once, stopped to think about what's like to live with a leg injury forever. I don't even care about the plot twist regarding the accident, because it doesn't excuse the fact that he never tried to put himself in Maggie's shoes. <br /><br />I didn't love Maggie either, I tried, oh I tried, but I don't understand how she can go from not even wanting to see Caleb, to him being the love she'll never forget. How can you date the guy who ran you over with a car and left you broken and bleeding and alone on the street?? Again, the twist doesn't really matter, because she dates him, makes out with him, falls in love with him way before knowing the truth. I don't get it. I honestly don't get it. <br /><br />I also don't understand how everyone at Maggie's school behaved like complete morons towards her. Seriously, a girl gets badly injured in an accident and everyone who knows her either ignores her or makes fun of her? Some of these guys even call her names like 'retard' because she limps... WTF? Where is this school exactly, Hell? I'm sorry but I don't think this is realistic at all. I've never, in my whole academic life, from the first grade to my final day at college, witnessed an injured/disabled person being bullied like that. I mean, I understand that this was just another thing to make Maggie's life even more sad and angsty, but in my opinion it's too much.<br /><br />One thing that I REALLY don't like in romance books is when one of the characters hooks up with someone else along the way, which Caleb does, he gets involved with his ex (who, by the way, he keeps complaining about, he doesn't like her lipstick or her perfume, her clothes are too revealing, and so on), they make out several times and apparently they have sex at some point too (there's no actual scene of the act--thank the gods for small mercies). This type of plot grosses me out and totally kills my mood to keep reading. How can I root for a couple when I'm told that one of the involved had sex with someone else <i>during</i> the couple's own slow burn romance journey? I can't.<br /><br />And then there's the plot twist regarding the accident, I'm not sure how I feel about it, but I can honestly say it didn't make me feel better about the love story, because, again: <b>I don't understand the romance. I don't understand Maggie.</b><br /><br />About the writing, the pace, and how the story unfolds: I was actually disappointed, because I've read <i>Perfect Chemistry</i> a while back, liked it a lot, and I don't remember complaining about any of this, but <b>Leaving Paradise</b> was kind of a mess--most of the important scenes are too rushed, others are mostly dialogue, without descriptions of what the characters are doing or feeling, and I believe that this made it harder for me to connect with them and with the story.<br /><br />The ending was quite terrible. I don't even care that there's a sequel. It's just terrible. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8354651540487282273" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_223754413" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/223754413" />
    <a title="Rose" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3399699-rose"><img alt="Rose" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1386022874p2/3399699.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/223754413?book_show_action=true">Dec 02, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rose" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rose" href="/user/show/3399699-rose">Rose</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=grief">grief</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=coming-of-age">coming-of-age</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=crime">crime</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=drama">drama</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=great-premise-lacking-execution">great-premise-lacking-execution</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=tough-subjects">tough-subjects</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer223754413" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12261004512560867753"><b>Initial reaction:</b> I feel like I'm of two minds with this book. One part of me really liked some of the emotional roughness and exploration of difficult situations this story offered, both for Maggie and Caleb's experiences. At the same time, I feel like this book had a cumbersome way of showing these details, so much at times that my suspension of disbelief couldn't overlook points of dramatic convenience for the sequence of events. I know this story has a follow up but did it have to end with s</span>
  <span id="freeText12261004512560867753" style="display:none"><b>Initial reaction:</b> I feel like I'm of two minds with this book. One part of me really liked some of the emotional roughness and exploration of difficult situations this story offered, both for Maggie and Caleb's experiences. At the same time, I feel like this book had a cumbersome way of showing these details, so much at times that my suspension of disbelief couldn't overlook points of dramatic convenience for the sequence of events. I know this story has a follow up but did it have to end with so many parts in the air and too quickly resolved?<br /><br /><b>Full review:</b><br /><br />I know this review is going to sound like a (albeit, brief) rant, but for all intents, I actually did like a significant part of this book and I found myself eagerly continuing it without wanting to put it down. I just didn't think that Elkeles's writing was that strong or consistent through the work, the latter part of the novel really showcasing how rushed and underdeveloped all of the respective matters in this book actually were. The progression felt awesome and the characters emotionally connected in moments, but then it felt rushed to heck and back and underdeveloped in others.<br /><br />Caleb and Maggie both felt like realistic characters with strong central conflicts to me - which was one of the reasons I was initially drawn to this story. Caleb's just out of prison for hitting Maggie in a drunken hit and run accident, while Maggie's recovering from her injuries and feeling her world crash down around her as her initial plans to flee their hometown of Paradise end up falling through. It's when Maggie and Caleb end up interacting again (reluctantly) that both of them start changing in individual ways that are key to recuperating from the stigma and self-doubts that surround them. I feel like the story had moments where it really had points to make about it, but it didn't feel as deep as I'd hoped it would be, though it did feel genuine on the part of the characters and their interactions with each other. I liked watching their moments of growth where it was possible to really see them come to terms with everything that was going on and the clashes that were unique to their homes, school interactions, and personal challenges. Heck, I even found myself believing their relationship, though I would say that the conflicts surrounding that made me lose my suspension of disbelief more than a few times.<br /><br />Yet I had a major bone to pick as the story started marching towards its ending - it was throwing all of these kinds of curveballs for reveals, and I felt like they were just shoehorned into the book just before ending on a note that promised a continuation or potential resolution in a forthcoming book. Like - I honestly feel with all of the situations it did end up revealing, it deserved a path towards the resolution that didn't feel like a steep drop off in some respects. That was what somewhat ruined the experience of the book for me. I still want to see what happens in the follow-up book, but it doesn't make me want to jump right into the next story for anticipation because I feel like this ended so haphazard.<br /><br />I thought it was worth the time - both for the strong audiobook performance and for watching the relationships between the characters develop and evoke their struggles over time. Yet, I also think it could've been a stronger experience.<br /><br />Overall score: 2.5/5 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12261004512560867753" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_21685068" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/21685068" />
    <a title="Jennifer Wardrip" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1125613-jennifer-wardrip"><img alt="Jennifer Wardrip" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442657515p2/1125613.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/21685068?book_show_action=true">May 06, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer Wardrip" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer Wardrip" href="/user/show/1125613-jennifer-wardrip">Jennifer Wardrip</a>
      </span>

          marked it as to-read




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1125613-jennifer-wardrip?shelf=trt-posted-reviews">trt-posted-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1125613-jennifer-wardrip?shelf=lendle-spot-booked-copies-available">lendle-spot-booked-copies-available</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1125613-jennifer-wardrip?shelf=teen">teen</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1125613-jennifer-wardrip?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer21685068" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11085128760144656819">Reviewed by Randstostipher "tallnlankyrn" Nguyen for TeensReadToo.com<br/><br/>Two very different people are joined together by the most common yet dreadful experience. Both live in the town of Paradise, but for them it is nothing like the name. <br/><br/>Caleb Becker had spent time in juvenile detention for the crime of driving while intoxicated and accidentally hitting someone with his car. And now that he has done his time, Caleb is able to go home to his family and his girlfriend, if they are still together. Bu</span>
  <span id="freeText11085128760144656819" style="display:none">Reviewed by Randstostipher "tallnlankyrn" Nguyen for TeensReadToo.com<br /><br />Two very different people are joined together by the most common yet dreadful experience. Both live in the town of Paradise, but for them it is nothing like the name. <br /><br />Caleb Becker had spent time in juvenile detention for the crime of driving while intoxicated and accidentally hitting someone with his car. And now that he has done his time, Caleb is able to go home to his family and his girlfriend, if they are still together. But for Caleb, returning to Paradise isn't so easy. His mother is trying to act like nothing has happened, his sister hardly talks to anyone and has went from prep to goth, and his dad is just there. <br /><br />Maggie Armstrong was that innocent person that Caleb hit, and she's been living in her own prison, the hospital. Trying to get back her life, Maggie has been trying her best to walk right again. But during those times, the people who Maggie thought were her friends began to grow apart from her. It's bad enough that her mother is trying to make ends meet and trying to make Maggie happy, but since Paradise isn't such a big town, there's a greater chance of Maggie running into Caleb. <br /><br />For Caleb, it's much easier for him to gain his life back, since he was always the popular one -- but for Maggie, she's closer to the outside. But the one thing they both truly needed wasn't their old friends or their old lives, but each other. That one incident, that one thing that affected both of them, each in a different way, has caused a strong connection between them that they would never be able to ignore. <br /><br />LEAVING PARADISE was honestly an amazing story, and was wonderfully written to where whoever reads it will not be able to get the story out of their head. Simone Elkeles, author of the highly acclaimed HOW TO RUIN A SUMMER VACATION, has switched gears and made an issue that is so common her own and very unique. The relationship between Caleb and Maggie was so real and extremely heartwarming, and the ways that they struggled to continue their lives, both individually and together, makes you wonder if you are able to be as strong as they are. <br /><br />This is another wonderful novel from Simone Elkeles, and I cannot wait to read her future publications.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12978353284339880205">Simone Elkeles knocked this book out of the park. Leaving Paradise is wonderful, the second half particularly stood out to me. Once I picked it up, I read for four hours straight to finish it. It's a lot more emotionally draining than Perfect Chemistry so if you're looking for that witty banter, you won't find it here. Leaving Paradise will put your heart through the ringer. Their relationship morphs from them individually having broken spirits to developing this strong attraction to facing pain</span>
  <span id="freeText12978353284339880205" style="display:none">Simone Elkeles knocked this book out of the park. Leaving Paradise is wonderful, the second half particularly stood out to me. Once I picked it up, I read for four hours straight to finish it. It's a lot more emotionally draining than Perfect Chemistry so if you're looking for that witty banter, you won't find it here. Leaving Paradise will put your heart through the ringer. Their relationship morphs from them individually having broken spirits to developing this strong attraction to facing painful heartbreak. This story also touches on the power of forgiveness and learning to trust.. That said, I did have a problem or two with one "conflict" and her name is Kendra. The other thing I must mention is the slow beginning but I forgive that for the amazing second half.<br /><br />I just want to go back and reread some passages from this now. I'm on the edge of my seat eagerly awaiting the sequel because that was a cruel cliffhanger.<br /><br />4.5 stars!<br /><br />*7/25/11 Recently reread and reviewed on <a href="http://www.witandfancy.com/2011/07/25/leaving-paradise-simone-elkeles/" rel="nofollow noopener">Wit &amp; Fancy</a>.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3570727581743745319">How you feel about yourself, family, friends and home can change after just one event, one night, and one mistake. How do you forgive and move on when that one mistake caused physical suffering and pain so embedded in your heart you cannot even admit it is there? Where do we even begin?   <span id="freeText3570727581743745319" style="display:none">How you feel about yourself, family, friends and home can change after just one event, one night, and one mistake. How do you forgive and move on when that one mistake caused physical suffering and pain so embedded in your heart you cannot even admit it is there? Where do we even begin? Maybe it takes our worlds completely shattering for us to see the pieces in a whole new way--the pieces and people right in front of us or right next door.<br /><br />Yes, Leaving Paradise has one of my biggest weaknesses—that boy next door! I can never resist a falling-for-the-boy-next-door story! I tell ya—I have been living in all the wrong places! :) Where are these boys?<br /><br />Caleb and Maggie’s story was so heartbreaking and compelling. The idea that the one person who hurt you the most could be the only person to help you heal really hit home for me. They both were such strong, likeable characters with electric chemistry together!<br /><br />This was a very addictive read, so be sure to have Return to Paradise on hand. I could not put it down!<br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_273629875" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/273629875?book_show_action=true">Feb 07, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erin" href="/user/show/4979538-erin">Erin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone in need of a beautiful love story!</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4979538-erin?shelf=romance-erotica-faves">romance-erotica-faves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4979538-erin?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer273629875" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13852361790175464907">This was a beautiful book! I literally read it in just a few hours because I could not put it down, then went immediately to my kindle to read Return to Paradise because I just had to hear more of their love story. This book has been out for awhile and has a ton of reviews already, so I'm not going to write much for that reason alone. I can not say enough how much I recommend it, though, because the message it sends and the heartwarming love story we get to experience are both unbelievably movin</span>
  <span id="freeText13852361790175464907" style="display:none">This was a beautiful book! I literally read it in just a few hours because I could not put it down, then went immediately to my kindle to read Return to Paradise because I just had to hear more of their love story. This book has been out for awhile and has a ton of reviews already, so I'm not going to write much for that reason alone. I can not say enough how much I recommend it, though, because the message it sends and the heartwarming love story we get to experience are both unbelievably moving. I adored Caleb and Maggie, these characters will hold a special place in my heart. I love reading stories like this, because it makes you look at things from a different perspective and forces you to at least try and grasp why people feel what they do. Leaving Paradise is a thought-provoking, real, butterfly-enducing story that I will never forget.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13852361790175464907" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('GThQSRQLQQQLLS2cqEhOHT5A++y//Du8chbkfiXVkjMjHjmbr1WIbKwGmf1fvUTC6B8cJHFxtdspaKLP6JZgqQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer2317635694625100790">Simone Elkeles is a <i>New York Times</i> and <i>USA Today</i> bestselling author of novels for teens. Simone’s books have won many awards including being YALSA Top Ten Quick Picks for Reluctant Young Adult Readers, being named to the YALSA Popular Paperbacks and Teens Top Ten lists, and added to the Illinois “Read for a Lifetime” Reading List. Simone also won the coveted RITA award from the Romance Writers of </span>
  <span id="freeText2317635694625100790" style="display:none">Simone Elkeles is a <i>New York Times</i> and <i>USA Today</i> bestselling author of novels for teens. Simone’s books have won many awards including being YALSA Top Ten Quick Picks for Reluctant Young Adult Readers, being named to the YALSA Popular Paperbacks and Teens Top Ten lists, and added to the Illinois “Read for a Lifetime” Reading List. Simone also won the coveted RITA award from the Romance Writers of America for her book Perfect Chemistry. Simone is especially proud of the fact that the Illinois Association of Teachers of English named her Author of the Year. <br /><br />Simone was born and raised in the suburbs of Chicago, where she still lives today. Simone went to the University of Illinois in Urbana-Champaign and received her Bachelor’s of Science there in Psychology in 1992. She continued her education at Loyola University-Chicago where she received her Master’s of Science degree in Industrial Relations while working for a manufacturing company creating diversity programs for their employees.<br /><br />She loves animals (she has two dogs – a labradoodle and a German Shepherd), kids (she also has two of those) and her family. In her spare time she’s the Hockey Mom for her kids hockey teams and is an active Girl Scout leader specially trained in outdoor education. She also spends time mentoring other teen and adult authors. (She also loves sushi, which you can probably tell by reading her books.) Simone writes about teens because she was a teen in the 80’s (when spiked hair and blue eye shadow were “rad”) and she loves writing about those exciting teen relationships and romances.</span>

</div>
</div>
